Opening of the German Socialist Party Congress, Hitler Issues a Declaration

Criticizing the Parliamentary Principles of Democracy

Implying That Federalism Cannot Exist

Determined to Fight Marxism to the End

Chancellor Hitler's lengthy declaration, written for the German Socialist Party Congress held here today, clarifies the Chancellor's future plans in general, without referring to foreign affairs. It reiterated the evils of Marxism, stating that Germany narrowly escaped a Bolshevik reign of terror at the beginning of this year, and pledged to continue the fight until those who poison the German people are completely eliminated. The most important issue today is the placement of the unemployed, which requires great effort. The declaration also criticized the parliamentary principles of democracy, stating that the will of the entire nation is the best tool for the government. The end of the declaration implied that the number of states in the federal system would be reduced, stating that the only pillar of the nation is the people and National Socialism, not the federal states. When Hitler and other National Socialist Party leaders arrived today, the audience waved swastika flags and warmly welcomed them. (One-day Reuters dispatch)

The German National Socialist Party Congress in Nuremberg officially opened this morning. Chancellor Hitler personally attended. Hess, chairman of the Central Committee of the National Socialist Party, represented Hitler in asking the audience to stand in memory of the martyrs. Then, Captain Röhm, chief of staff of the National Socialist Party's Storm Troopers, delivered a speech commemorating the deaths and injuries of armed comrades of the National Socialist Party. Subsequently, Hess paid tribute to foreign guests, especially expressing admiration for the representatives of Fascist Italy, and stated that Germany is loyal to peace and that its only goal is to achieve security for countries that do not yet have common sense. The speech concluded by praising Hitler, calling him "the guarantor of final victory." (One-day Havas dispatch)

The German National Socialist Party Congress in Nuremberg discussed foreign fascist movements. The leader of the National Socialist Party in China, Hasenjuer (General Manager of Zen Cheong & Co. in Shanghai), explained the situation of National Socialism and Germanism abroad. The congress decided that the National Socialist Party's foreign Germanism branch will be under the control of Hess from now on. (Hess is the chairman of the Central Committee of the National Socialist Party and presided over the congress on behalf of Chancellor Hitler before its official opening.) Subsequently, Dietrich, the director of the National Socialist Party's Information Bureau, gave a speech to representatives of the German and foreign press, saying that foreigners find it difficult to understand the National Socialist Party movement because it is not an intellectual movement but a movement from the people. He also asked the press to build a bridge between the old liberal concepts and the new concepts of the authoritarian state in order to communicate with each other and seek better international understanding. He then recounted the struggle of the National Socialist Party against the republican system established by the Weimar Constitution and the destruction of Hitlerism by the old system. Dietrich also praised Hitler, saying, "A man was born to represent the National Socialist Party movement. No head of state in any country has received such popular support as Hitler. It is said that 'faith can move mountains,' and I say that faith in Hitler can move mountains. Those who rule Germany today are neither emperors nor tyrants, but the great personality of Hitler." (One-day Havas dispatch)

Hitler arrived in Nuremberg today to attend his first National Socialist Party Congress since becoming dictator. The enthusiastic welcome he received surpassed that of even Caesar in the past. The entire city was filled with flags and banners, and portraits of Hitler and swastikas were everywhere. Members of the Brownshirts filled the streets, and hotels and accommodations within thirty miles were fully booked. The mayor delivered a speech welcoming Hitler, calling him a fearless and pure knight. The entire city presented Hitler with a sculpture by the famous artist Dürer, which was engraved with the words "Knight, Death, Devil," referring to Hitler's work in destroying the devil, which is Marxism. Thousands of women came from afar, hoping to listen to Hitler's speech on the role of women in the National Socialist Party movement, but the meeting was suddenly canceled without explanation. Many of the women returned disappointed, and many wept. 60,000 members of the youth league traveled here by free transport, hoping to listen to Hitler's inspiring speech on Sunday. The National Socialist Party Congress is scheduled to open tomorrow, at which time Hitler will attend and detail the progress of the National Socialist Party movement. (31st Reuters dispatch)

Another New Hero is About to Arrive

Alois Hudal, the Austrian National Socialist Party leader, was rescued from prison and escaped to Italy. He will now be a new hero of this National Socialist Party Congress. Tomorrow, Hudal and the person who rescued him from prison will arrive here by plane. More than 100,000 members of the National Socialist Party plan to give them a warm welcome. (31st Reuters dispatch)

Göring Promoted to General

Deeply Trusted by Hindenburg

(Berlin) President Hindenburg promoted Göring, the Prussian Prime Minister and German Aviation Minister, to General of the Infantry in Prussia to commemorate his achievements in saving Germany. This move was unexpected and shows the depth of President Hindenburg's trust and reliance on Göring. According to past history, there have been only two cases of low-ranking German officers being promoted to general in one step. One was the Iron Chancellor Bismarck, who was promoted from major to general, and the other was Chancellor Hollweg, who was appointed by former German Emperor Wilhelm II. (30th Reuters dispatch)

It is not right to consider them deserters." He also attacked the increase in expenditure due to the recruitment of civil defense forces in Austria. Once Austria falls into the hands of the National Socialist Party, the people of the Germanic race and their officials will enjoy happiness and freedom." (One-day Havas dispatch)

(London) Professor Einstein, in his capacity as Chairman of the International Committee, today released the "German Terror Brown Book," which contains 250 cases of murder by the National Socialist Party since the beginning of March this year, as well as photographs of German atrocities such as flogging dissidents. The US Industrial Recovery Regulations Begin to Take Effect

Roosevelt Relaxes on the Beach

Confident That the Experiment Will Be Successful

(Washington) Starting at midnight tonight, the National Industrial Recovery Administration will begin implementing its grand plan to control the national industry and commerce. All industrial codes of conduct and industry regulations will take effect at this time. It is now set that the sound of factory whistles across the country tomorrow morning will be the starting point for the US President's new enterprise, and the official start of his efforts to raise prices, wages, and living standards, and to shorten working hours. Some cities will hold official celebrations at this time, such as Detroit, the center of the automobile industry. This whistle will mark the eradication of child labor in mechanical work as a thing of the past, and the official start of what many consider to be a radical and dangerous experiment by the government. Roosevelt, who is in charge of this matter, is confident that success can be expected with the support of 80% of the national industry and commerce. At this time, he is relaxing on a yacht, vacationing on the New England coast. (31st National Dispatch)

Extension of the Deadline for the Public to Surrender Hoarded Gold

(Washington) Today, Washington officialdom is still busy resolving the gold issue, wanting hoarders to return their gold to the treasury. However, the officialdom has not explained why the US government has suddenly stepped up this activity. The deadline for the public to return gold, originally set for September 12, has now been extended to September 18. Attorney General Cummings has already left the capital, and officials in his department are unwilling to disclose the reason for the extension. (31st National Dispatch)

Labor Issues Encounter Resistance

(Washington) Officials in the National Recovery Administration have publicly disagreed on how to handle labor disputes. Three members of the executive committee have now resigned, including General Johnson's deputy, Mr. Caho, because Caho opposes the Workers' Rights labor policy, considering it provocative and contrary to the spirit of the recovery plan. Caho advocates the creation of direct labor unions, under the approval and protection of the government, to seek the interests of workers, employers, and consumers. General Johnson acknowledged today that some officials will be dismissed. The Recovery Administration is now past the experimental stage, and temporary regulations have been approved for eight industries, such as the telecommunications industry, the radio broadcasting industry, and the silk industry. The silk industry strike has been resolved through the mediation of the National Labor Board. (One-day Reuters dispatch)

(Washington) Some coal mine owners are now rejecting the new industry regulations, and the number of silk industry workers on strike in Paterson, New Jersey, has now reached 40,000. Although the work of the National Recovery Administration is still actively underway, resistance often occurs. The Public Works Department will hand over $70 million to the Army Department today for river and port engineering projects. President Roosevelt will have the power to enforce various industry regulations under the recovery plan starting the day after tomorrow. It is rumored that Ford, which accounts for a quarter of the total automobile industry, will seek another industry regulation or seek legal remedies to resist unconstitutional interference with the rights of individual employers. (31st Reuters dispatch)

Two Small Towns on the Pacific Coast

The Mexican Government Opens Free Ports

Foreign Goods Imported are Exempt from Taxes

As an Experiment to Promote Commerce

Mexico City The Mexican President today issued an executive order opening the towns of Tijuana and Ensenada as free ports, exempting all foreign goods imported from all taxes. Tijuana is 16 miles from San Diego, USA, with a highway to Baja California. Ensenada is on the Pacific coast, about 100 miles from San Diego. It is only a small town. A few years ago, even the people of California in the United States often did not know its name. Usually, only some livestock and agricultural products enter and leave its port. The Mexican Ministry of Commerce hopes to develop the northwest coast and conduct an experiment on whether tariffs are not entirely beneficial, so it proposed this proposal, which led to today's order. Domestic workers and a part of businessmen have tried their best to oppose this move, fearing that the national industry and commerce will be monopolized by foreigners. If not, they also oppose the Mexican government's plan to generally reduce tariffs and promote commerce, but the Ministry of Commerce believes that with the Foreign Land Law in place, there is no risk of foreigners monopolizing industries. Mexico advocated generally reducing tariffs at the World Economic Conference. When this proposal failed, the Mexican President proposed that Mexico independently reduce tariffs to promote foreign trade, but there was strong opposition in the country. Today, it was decided to first conduct an experiment of opening free ports. A government spokesman said that if the implementation is not seen to be beneficial, it will not be difficult to correct it. (31st National Dispatch)

Italy and Russia Sign a Non-Aggression Pact

Comments from Roman Newspapers

All Roman newspapers have commented on the upcoming signing of the Italo-Russian non-aggression pact. They all said that the agreement is obviously a continuation of the Four-Power Pact. "The Italian Daily" said that the Italo-Russian treaty is actually a procedural agreement on security, the main points of which are similar to the agreements that the Soviet Union previously signed with other countries, namely: 1. Mutual non-aggression; 2. If one of the contracting parties has a conflict with a third country, the other contracting party shall remain neutral; 3. No economic sanctions shall be used; 4. If disputes arise between the contracting parties that cannot be resolved through normal diplomatic channels, mediation procedures shall be applied. The newspaper also said, "This treaty does not create any new facts except to consolidate the existing position and potentially develop politically in Europe which is highly interconnected." The Forum newspaper said, "Once this treaty is concluded, it shows that two countries with different ideals and political systems can engage in beneficial economic and political cooperation to maintain peace." "The Party Labour Report" said, "Since Italy recognized the Soviet Union, relations between the two countries have been extremely friendly. The new treaty cannot change this, but it can be regarded as a result of the basic principles of Italian policy, and further evidence of the Soviet Union seeking international cooperation in a peaceful spirit." (31st Havas Dispatch)

Ecuadorian President Fully Contains the Bud of Rebellion

Various Trade Unions Were Searched and Seized by the Military Police

National 31st Guayaquil Dispatch The Ecuadorian government used swift means to contain the bud of rebellion. The military police here, under the order of the President, suddenly searched and seized various trade unions this morning. Yesterday, workers in various industries only stopped working and returned to their homes, declaring that they would not go to work again unless the President resigned. Afterwards, although the President issued a notice to resume work, the situation this morning seemed to have not made any impression on the workers.

The Penang Assembly Proposes to Improve Chinese Weddings

Different Customs and Different Customs

Overseas Chinese in Malaya Mostly Hold Different Opinions

Reuters 1st Singapore Dispatch A Chinese member of the Penang Legislative Council, Mr. Lin, proposed that the government implement an order to improve the weddings of non-Muslim and non-Christian Chinese. It is said that overseas Chinese in Malaya have many different opinions on this proposal. According to the intention of Councilor Lin, it is still questionable whether the courts consider the improved wedding ceremony proposed by the new Chinese school to be legal. Therefore, it is better for the government to promulgate the wedding ceremony. Overseas Chinese born in Nanyang and those from China are paying close attention to this matter. Although many people do not oppose the old-fashioned wedding, they believe that the improved wedding should be considered legal by the court. At the same time, the majority oppose the government promulgating the wedding ceremony, because overseas Chinese in Malaya come from different places and have different customs. Not only are the wedding ceremonies very different, but also the procedures before and after engagement to marriage are different from each other. Overseas Chinese have their own local customs for hundreds of years. If they are suddenly interfered with, it should not be done by a wise man. Overseas Chinese public organizations are now planning to request the government to abide by the old rules, and the court will consult the opinions of overseas Chinese leaders as usual when there are questions about legality.

Petition of Representatives of Heze Flood Victims

Going to Jinan to See Han, then to Beijing

The Relief Committee Repeatedly Telegraphs for Aid

Jinan Dispatch: The disaster situation in western Shandong is dire. Chairman Han has repeatedly telegraphed the central government to report the situation and request relief. However, the central government's relief funds have been slow to arrive. The provincial government has specially dispatched Director of Education He Siyuan, as a representative to go to Beijing to report the disaster situation and urge the allocation of relief funds. He departed for Beijing this morning (31st) with representatives of the flood victims from Heze. Furthermore, Sun Zirang, the magistrate of Heze County, yesterday submitted a report to the Shandong Rural Construction Research Institute, detailing the disaster situation in the county, with every word filled with tears, making it unbearable to read.

One of the Tragic Scenes of the Floods in Western Shandong and Southern Hebei: Villages Submerged, Houses Collapsed

Sun also telegraphed Zhang Hanying, a member and Secretary-General of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, stating that the upstream water level was still rising and requesting that he quickly arrange for the breaching to be blocked. The Heze County flood victim representatives Ge Xiangyi, Yan Junqing, Ran Jiwu, and others arrived in Jinan on the 30th and today (31st) met with Provincial Government Chairman Han Fuqu, reported the disaster situation, and submitted a petition for immediate relief and speedy closure of the breach. According to Ge Xiangyi, "The scale of this flood is unprecedented in previous floods. More than 1,500 villages in Heze County have been submerged (800 villages completely submerged and 700 villages partially submerged). 350,000 flood victims are immersed in water. The old grain has been washed away, and the new grain has not yet been harvested. They have no clothes and no food. They want to flee but cannot because the county was originally land-based and has no boats. Now it is suddenly a vast ocean, and they cannot move, trapped in the water, crying for food. For example, when we set off from Heze this time, we first detoured southeast to Nanyang Lake, taking boats twice in between, and wading through the mud for more than ten miles. Finally, we took a boat from Nanyang Lake up the Grand Canal to Jining, a distance of 230 miles, taking six days in total. The difficulty of the journey is evident. Everywhere we looked, it was a vast ocean, houses collapsed, a tragic sight," and so on. This morning (31st) at 6:30, led by Director of Education He Siyuan, the representatives went to Jinde Hall to meet with Han. Han first asked about the situation in the disaster area. The representatives reported in detail, roughly saying, "Now the water level sometimes rises and sometimes falls, and the entire county is submerged. We have come to petition for three things: immediate relief, speedy closure of the breach, and a fundamental solution to the flood problem in western Shandong. Since the sixth year of the Republic, the Yellow River has breached in Hebei Province 15 times, flooding western Shandong each time. The reason is that the soil quality on both banks of the Yellow River in northern Hebei is poor, and those managing the river are territorial, thinking that even if there is a breach, it will not flood Hebei Province, so they do not pay much attention. This has led to repeated breaches. Without a fundamental solution, the people of western Shandong will suffer from flooding every year. The current flow is from the string ditch outside the Fanzhuang breach. Therefore, this string ditch must be blocked first so that it does not flow. After the disaster area dries up, wheat can be planted. When the water level drops in autumn and winter, blocking the breach will be easy. The flowing string ditch is only 50 li long. If Hebei Province had blocked this ditch first, there would have been no breach this time. Now, the three breaches on the south bank, the Fanzhuang breach in Changyuan County, are flooding western Shandong, the Kaocheng breach is flooding Cao County and Shan County, and the Lanfeng breach is also affecting Cao and Shan. The Chairman previously sent armored vehicles to Jining to pick up flood victims, which we are very grateful for, but because there are no boats, they cannot reach Jining and can only sigh in despair."

Han then replied, roughly saying, "Hearing you speak of the suffering of the flood victims, it is very pitiful. The provincial government will do its best to provide relief. When you go to Beijing, you must also speak out. I will definitely report my opinions to the central government: 1. Immediate relief; 2. Closing the breach; 3. The area south of the Yellow River in Dongming County could be transferred to Henan Province so that the authority to manage the river is unified; 4. There must be a comprehensive plan for both temporary and permanent solutions," and so on. The representatives then took their leave and boarded a train at 9:00, accompanied by He Siyuan, to go to Beijing.

The Relief Committee telegraphed Beijing again, requesting that national taxes be retained for disaster relief, stating: "To Chairman Lin of the Nanjing National Government, Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan, Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission, and Chairman Xu Jun of the Relief Committee: The floods in western Shandong have led to repeated telegraphs for relief. We have recently learned that Chairman Jiang has replied to the provincial government, saying that the loan of American wheat and cotton to China is uncertain and cannot be used. Therefore, Shandong Province is not allocated any cotton or wheat. Regarding the Shandong relief funds, the Ministry of Finance stopped issuing them last winter. The income from the customs surtax for the 20th year of the Republic for disaster relief was originally intended to be distributed to the disaster-stricken provinces, a certain amount of income per year, but Shandong has not received a single cent. In the 19th year, the government explicitly ordered the compensation of the disaster-stricken counties in Shandong, ranging from 20,000 to 30,000 yuan per county, but in the end, not a single penny was distributed. The national army requisitioned local areas in each county to the tune of 3 to 4 million, which the government has not yet repaid and is entirely borne by the local areas. The relief funds donated by overseas Chinese for the May 3rd Tragedy in the 17th year were transferred by the government for other purposes and were not remitted to Shandong. This is the true situation of the government's disaster relief and management measures for the people of Shandong over the years. The tax obligations of the people of Shandong to the government have been increasing over the years. For example, the salt tax alone has increased from 5 million to more than 11 million yuan. The government has allocated salt permits to various provinces to pay taxes for the lost territories in the Northeast, adding 2 yuan and 8 jiao per stone, while Shandong's own laws add 4 yuan per dan, which the central government also collects into the national treasury. This is the true situation of the government's demand for our people's tax obligations over the years. The government takes from the people for fear of not taking enough and is stingy in giving to the people. Looking around hesitantly, we knew early on that a major change would occur.

One of the Tragic Scenes of the Floods in Western Shandong and Southern Hebei: Refugees on the Dike Crying for Food

Inevitably, we will be helpless. After the Ministry of Finance stopped issuing relief funds, we repeatedly telegraphed the government, requesting that it comply with Sun Yat-sen's Founding Program, allowing us to retain no more than 50% of the national tax revenue to handle local charitable undertakings, allowing us to retain a portion to assist local relief efforts, and requesting that the 4 yuan per stone of salt permits under the Shandong Single Regulations, which is not an income stipulated by central law, be allowed to be intercepted by this province to serve as relief funds. The government found it difficult to approve, and so it continues to this day. Now, the Lanfeng breach has flooded western Shandong, affecting as many as eighteen or nine counties, submerging hundreds of thousands of people. The dead are gone, but what about the living? They cry out in desperation, begging for salvation. There is no rice to cook, and they only cry out in vain. We earnestly beseech your Excellency to have compassion for the severity of the flood disaster in Shandong Province and grant a special favor, allowing us to temporarily borrow one million yuan from the Shandong national tax revenue or allowing us to retain 10% to provide relief. We are most eagerly awaiting your orders. Zhao Xinru, Standing Committee Member of the Shandong Provincial Relief Committee, kowtows with tears." (31st)

Page 15

A Visit to Feng at Mount Tai

Feng Expresses No Intention of Going to Beijing

His Daily Life Consists of Early to Bed, Early to Rise

His Anti-Japanese Ambition Remains Steadfast

Jinan Dispatch: This reporter went to Tai'an the other day and climbed Mount Tai on the 30th to visit Mr. Feng Yuxiang. At 10:00 a.m. that morning, Feng received me at the Xixin Pavilion near the Five Sages Shrine. Feng was wearing a white cloth short shirt and pants, blue cloth socks, and black shoes. His hair was quite long and untrimmed. This reporter first asked about Chen Gongbo's recent visit on behalf of Wang Jingwei to invite Mr. Feng to Beijing and what Mr. Feng's opinion was. Feng said that he had met with Chen on the 29th and that Chen's visit was a personal expression of concern. The so-called invitation on behalf of Wang to invite him to Beijing was entirely speculation. Recently, Sun Zhesheng and other friends have come to Tai'an to strongly advise him to go to Beijing, but he has no intention of going to Beijing recently. I then asked what Mr. Feng thought about the central government giving him the position of Water Conservancy Superintendent. Feng said that he had not heard anything about it and had no opinion to express. Feng continued to talk about how the tariff barriers of various countries in the world were increasing day by day, and people were suffering from poverty, illness, and death. Although Japan is now invading our country, it is only a perverse phenomenon, driven by the ambition of a few warlords. Its people are also bound to suffer from poverty, illness, and death. Bihana once said that occupying the three northeastern provinces of our country is like holding a bomb in one's mouth. To become a second Germany. In my opinion, it is not just a bomb, but a landmine, because our country has 470 million people, while Japan only has 60 or 70 million. Wouldn't that be a huge mess for them? Now, to seek true right and wrong, one can only find it in the countryside and towns. There is no true right and wrong in the provincial capital, let alone in the nation. They reverse black and white and replace truth with falsehood. Last year, I carved an essay on Mozi's "Against Aggression" at Xishan, and I was truly moved when I wrote it. His words were filled with emotion.

This reporter happened to read the anti-Japanese texts carved on the stone corridor around the Xixin Pavilion, which read, "Have you forgotten? The three northeastern provinces have been occupied by the Japanese. Those with backbone should risk their lives to take them back." The inscription indicates the area and population of the three provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang. This was carved by Feng last year. Feng then pointed to it and said, "It can't be used now, because since last year until now, more than ten months have passed, and we have also lost the province of Rehe, losing millions of people. What a great sigh!" This reporter also asked about Feng's daily life on Mount Tai. Feng said, "I get up at dawn, go to bed early and get up early, which also saves lamp oil. After getting up, I write six large characters. After washing, I eat porridge and then walk 6,000 steps on the nearby hillside until I am covered in sweat. I start classes at 7:00. Before noon, I read social sciences, and at 11:00 I receive guests. At 12:00, I have breakfast, and after a short rest, I watch the news at 2:00. At 4:00, I discuss the Spring and Autumn Annals with Mr. Fan Mingshu and others. After continuing to discuss the Zuo Zhuan at 6:00, I speak to the soldiers. At 7:00, I have dinner, and at 9:00, I rest. My family has recently come to Mount Tai completely." At this point, this reporter asked Feng to write a calligraphy. Feng immediately took a brush and wrote two couplets, one being "Saving the people knows no day of rest; Revolution knows no limit." and the other being "To be free from troubles, one must have no self; To make a good person, one must go through hardships." Underneath, he wrote Feng Yuxiang and stamped it with a seal with the two characters "San Hu" (Three Households). Feng then explained that "Three Households" was enough to destroy Qin. Now our country has 470 million compatriots. Why can't we destroy Japan? Feng's unwavering anti-Japanese ambition is evident here. Then Feng gave the reporter several copies of the publication "From Yuge River to Mount Tai." It is said that Feng is also writing books such as "From Mount Tai to Chahar," "The Beginning and End of Anti-Japanese Resistance in Chahar," and "From Chahar Back to Mount Tai," which are currently being printed. (31st)

He Bandit is Rampant Again

Songzi, Shimen, and Fen Counties Under Heavy Attack

Xu Yuanquan Orders All Armies to Encircle and Suppress Them Forcefully

Hankou Dispatch: He Long's remnant bandits, previously fleeing from western Hubei to Hunan, were in dire straits. The Five Crane bandit nests were successively recovered by Xu Yuanquan's troops. It was thought that the rifles had been swept away and that pacification was imminent. Unexpectedly, after the bandits retreated to the Hunan border, they suddenly split into two groups, one advancing towards Shifeng in Hunan and the other fleeing back towards Songzi in Hubei, both being extremely rampant. The local militias in each county were not sufficient to withstand their onslaught. According to reports, Shimen and Fen counties were under critical attack, and the county magistrates were tenaciously defending them while telegraphing the province for assistance. The magistrate of Songzi County was seriously injured while leading troops to suppress the bandits, and there are reports that he has been killed in action. The rampant nature of the bandit forces can be imagined. Initially, the bandits mostly fled into Hunan via Yexiong Pass in Laifeng, intending to attack Yongshun, Sangzhi, and Dayong with full force. Therefore, the bandit suppression troops were all concentrated in that area for encirclement and suppression. He Long knew that his situation was desperate and did not dare to resist the national army. He gathered the bandit leaders Xia Xi, He Ying, Liu Kexi, He Xianggu, He Mangu, and others, reorganized the remnants of the pseudo-7th, 8th, 9th, and 3rd Divisions, as well as the guard division, training regiment, and guerrillas, into two routes, and led them east in secret, harassing Songzi, Zhijiang, Shimen, and Fen counties. This was because there were the fewest stationed troops and the weakest local defense forces there, so they avoided the strong and attacked the weak. Xu Yuanquan, the commander-in-chief of bandit suppression in the Hunan-Hubei border area, returned to Shashi from Hankou the other day. He originally planned to depart for Enshi to supervise the suppression, but now that the remnant bandits have fled east, he has stopped his trip. He has also ordered the various brigades of the directly subordinate 48th Division, as well as the independent 38th Brigade of Pan Shanzhai, the newly compiled 3rd Brigade of Jiang Zuojun, the various units of the provincial security team of Zhang Gang, and the troops of Chen Quzhen's newly compiled 34th Division of the Hunan Army, to encircle and suppress them in various ways, determined to wipe them out. According to observations by the authorities, the bandits originally had a strength of about 15,000 men. Since the division of Duan Dechang and Wang Bingnan's forces, they have no more than 10,000 men. In the current suppression by Xu's army, the bandits suffered heavy losses in the battles of Hefeng, Shihui Yao, Hongtu Xi, Xi Dui Ping, Guanyin Ping, and Wuyang Guan. Only a few thousand men remain, and spanning Hunan and Hubei, their strength is divided, making it difficult for them to withstand a major army assault. Even if they can cause trouble for a while, it is only a last-ditch effort.

Regarding the issue of post-war reconstruction in western Hubei, Commander-in-Chief Chiang had previously instructed the provincial government to prepare for it. Provincial Chairman Zhang Qun has submitted it for discussion at the meeting, and the entire committee has decided to draft a plan. The four departments of civil affairs, finance, construction, and education, as well as the security office, are also drafting measures within their respective areas of responsibility. Generally, in terms of civil affairs, the goal is to provide disaster relief to the victims, recruit refugees, manage Qingxiang, compile and check Baojia, and in terms of finance, it is to raise and allocate relief funds, clean up taxes, unify the tax system, eliminate long-standing malpractices, and in terms of construction, it is to build roads, and in terms of education, it is to strictly implement social education, and in terms of security, such as reorganizing militias and strengthening the people's self-defense forces, and with the ultimate common goal being rural revival and social stability. However,

Western Hubei includes more than a dozen counties including Yichang, Yidu, Songzi, Zhijiang, Changyang, Zigui, Badong, Wufeng, Hefeng, Laifeng, Xianfeng, Xuanen, Enshi, Lichuan, and Jianshi. The area is vast, and the cost is high. It is rumored that the emergency relief funds are tentatively set at 20,000 yuan, which is truly inadequate. Even the work-relief funds are only using the 150,000 yuan allocated by the headquarters, which is also likely to be insufficient. Therefore, the issue of funds will require a great deal of planning. (August 31st)

Inspection Record of Jiangxi, Anhui, Hunan, and Hubei by Our Newspaper's Special Correspondent Ren An

Oppressive Taxes and Miscellaneous Levies and the Blockade of Bandit Areas

Special Dispatch from Yichun: The bandit situation in Yichun is still quite serious, so frequent taxes are unavoidable. According to what Liu District Chief of the First District and Ouyang Yuanren said, the amount of burden borne by the people is always proportional to the distance from the bandit area. The closer to the bandit area, the more severely they are harmed by the bandits, and the greater the responsibility they bear for assisting in the suppression. Taking the grain tax in each district as an example, the First District, near the city, is located in a safe area, and the tax is calculated as 4 yuan for rice converted into cash, 3 yuan for land tax per liang, and surcharges of 9 jiao for education, construction, and autonomy, 1 jiao for handling fees, 6 yuan for defense funds, and 3 yuan for volunteer fees, totaling 17 yuan. In other districts, some pay more than 20 yuan. The Fifth District and others pay almost 40 yuan. The Sixth District is entirely a bandit area (the county Soviet of the bandit army is located in Cihua Town in that district. All the expenses required by the defense regiment and volunteers, the so-called "wool comes from the sheep's back," are generally levied by force from the banditized people. In total, the annual expenses for volunteers, etc., levied along with the grain in the First, Second, Third, and Fourth Districts are about 13,000 to 15,000 yuan, more than 15,000 yuan in the Eighth District, more than 20,000 yuan in the Seventh District, more than 30,000 yuan in the Fifth District, and uncertain in the Sixth District. On average, one liang per ding (labor), accounting for about 12 mu of land, can harvest 400 buckets of grain.

The landlord can collect 200 buckets of rent, worth 50 to 60 yuan. After paying the regular grain tax and surcharges, there is very little left. In addition, they must be subject to the same donations as tenants for building roads and repairing bridges. There are few who are not skinned alive. In the past, people wanted to achieve peace in the world, selling knives and buying cattle. Now, the general farmers who are suffering from soldiers, bandits, and taxes must sell cattle and buy knives to seek salvation. Reflecting on the past and present, I cannot help but feel emotional.

The county originally had more than 60 joint security offices and more than 600 individual security offices. Later, because most of the Baojia heads and Lianren (joint security chiefs) were ignorant and foolish people, also known locally as "they must be cunning rogues to be willing to do this job of sitting on benches" (the common name for Baojia heads among the villagers), they abused their power and exploited the villagers. Some levied gun-buying fees of at least 3 yuan per household without even issuing a receipt. Various malpractices are too numerous to mention. The villagers who could not bear the oppression rose up to protest and cry out in pain. At the same time, office expenses could not be raised, and most of the joint security offices have been reduced and merged.

The people have always been known to be strong and brave. At the end of the Qing Dynasty, when the new policies were being implemented, Lu Yuanbi, a local gentry, levied taxes under the guise of education. The farmers in the four villages rose up in rebellion, carrying spears and knives, besieging the county seat for thirteen days and nights. When they heard that Lu had been dismissed, the siege was lifted. In the 16th year of the Republic, Fu, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, conspired with the Party headquarters and other organizations to add a surcharge of 1 yuan and 5 jiao. The farmers also rioted and sent an army of retribution, swarming into the city in tens of thousands. In the end, they killed Fu and his accomplice Liu and burned down their houses before stopping. However, the people's performance on the other hand is quite generous. That is, in the event of major and minor disputes, the parties are often willing to prepare refreshments or set up a banquet, urging fair people to resolve the matter fairly, and rarely resort to suing in the county government. It is not without reason.

Ramie cloth is the most famous product. The method of manufacture is to first peel off the bast of the ramie stalk, soak it in water, and scrape off the coarse material with bamboo strips. Dry it over a gentle fire, which is called "beating ramie." Then, mix yellow cattle dung into the ramie for about three hours, take it out, wash it clean, and expose it to the sun on the green grass. After it is half-dry, sprinkle it with water slightly. After three or four days, the color is clean and white, even more beautiful than that bleached with bleaching powder, and it does not damage the toughness of the ramie. Some people use lime, but absolutely no bleaching powder is used, so as not to damage the toughness of the ramie. This is called "bleaching ramie." Then, "continuing ramie" is to meticulously and evenly connect the roots and tips of the ramie thread, preparing it for weaving. The female workers compete with each other in skill and beauty in continuing and weaving ramie, and they do not care about the time and effort it takes.

The blockade is being implemented here, with many terms and clauses. In a word, it is to sever all material exchanges and relations with the bandit area. Among them, kerosene and salt are particularly strictly prohibited. Each person is prescribed to eat three qian of salt per day. A family of five needs one liang and five qian. For kerosene, a household with five or fewer people is limited to two liang per day, six to ten people are limited to four liang, and more than ten people cannot exceed half a jin at most. If you want to store it, you are only allowed to store enough for three days. (August 16th)

Various Perspectives on the Decline of Pingxiang

Special Dispatch from Pingxiang: Pingxiang is a vital transportation hub between Jiangxi and Hunan provinces. To the west lies the Jiangxi-Hunan highway, leading directly to Nanchang; to the east is the Pingxiang-Zhuzhou railway, connecting to Changsha via Zhuzhou. Moreover, it boasts the Anyuan Coal Mine, whose products sell well in major ports along the Yangtze River. Other products such as Xia cloth, fireworks, and earthenware are also quite notable. It used to be known as a region with thriving industry and commerce. However, since 1930, the area has been plagued by the occupation of large bands of communist bandits, followed by the "banditization" of peasants and workers in the surrounding countryside. Years of military campaigns have imposed unbearable burdens, turning the wealthy into the poor, and the poor into bandits. The rural economy has been declining daily, and the commercial slump is becoming unsustainable. The major businesses in the city still strive to maintain their inventory and displays, but the few customers on the streets often just look and leave. When there are occasional customers, the surrounding shops compete to attract them. Taking Xia cloth shops as an example, in previous years, sales extended as far as the Northeast and Korea, with each store selling over a thousand yuan per day. Now, many shops do not make a single sale all day. The situation is even worse for fireworks, earthenware, and other products.

There used to be over 700 elementary and secondary schools for both boys and girls in Pingxiang, as well as rural compulsory education schools. The sources of educational funding were: (1) over 15,700 "shi" (a unit of dry measure, about 100 liters) of school land rent, (2) a surcharge on deed taxes, collecting 7.5 "li" (a unit of currency) per tael, amounting to about 2,000 yuan per year, (3) an annual subsidy of 8,000 yuan from the Anyuan Coal Mine Company. Now, over 3,000 "shi" of grain rent has fallen into bandit-controlled areas. The Anyuan Coal Mine Company has also stopped its subsidy due to recent operating losses. Furthermore, the original school land rent has been forcibly extracted by various district offices, volunteer corps, and Baojia (local security) units, even to the point of seizing silver from the land rent collection. The Education Bureau's school land rent used to buy guns, and the deducted land rent has already reached 1,000 "shi." Due to these reasons, school funding is lacking, and nearly 300 schools have been forced to close. Consequently, a request was made to the provincial government for permission to levy a coal tax of five cents per ton, which could generate 4,000 to 5,000 yuan per year to supplement the funding. However, after the Education Bureau had spent tremendous effort to get this approved the year before last, it aroused the envy of the Security Regiment, which then sent troops to take over the collection entirely. The coal merchants also anticipated that the Security Regiment's organization would not be permanent, and its term for collecting the tax would be shorter than the Education Bureau's, so they were happy to pay it. As a result, educational funding has been steadily shrinking, forcing the restriction of student enrollment and an 80% reduction in teachers' salaries. Elementary school teachers now earn only eight or nine yuan per month, and their living conditions are obviously dire.

Anyuan is located about ten "li" (a Chinese unit of distance, about 0.5 km) from the city. The Anyuan Coal Mine Company was founded in the twentieth year of the Guangxu Emperor's reign (1894) and is a large operation. Coal transportation, screening, and washing are all done by machines. It also has both native and foreign furnaces for producing coke. Coke has a very high temperature and melts iron very quickly. Ordinary coal sells for only six yuan per ton, while coke is worth eighteen or nineteen yuan. The total fixed assets of the plant are about six or seven million yuan. The mining area covers over thirty "li," and there are thirteen coal seams in total. During its peak in 1919 and 1920, the daily output was 3,000 to 4,000 tons, but now it is only 400 tons. The total reserves are not yet precisely known. Some say that it will be exhausted in another twenty years, while others say that what has been mined so far is only the coal outcrop, and the vast reserves have not yet been reached. There are two mine entrances. One goes horizontally into the mountain, with tunnels branching out for dozens of "li." All are lit by electric lights and use electric trains for transportation. In the Wangjiayuan and Zijia Chong mining areas, more than ten "li" away, underground electric trains are available for transportation. The Gaokeng mine, twenty "li" away, has extremely rich reserves, and the Ministry of Industry is preparing to exploit it. For the convenience of transportation between them, underground tunnels may also be connected. The other mine, called Bafangjing, has two shafts, each about eight feet in diameter, twenty feet apart, and 160 "fa chi" (a unit of length) deep. Entry and exit are done using elevators, which move up and down, very quickly. The coal reserves are abundant, and the coal quality is excellent. Engineers say that if they go another fifty "fa chi" deeper, there will be even larger reserves. Unfortunately, the great flood of 1931 completely submerged the entire mine's resources. To restore it, it would cost no less than seventy or eighty thousand yuan. In the past, coal sales were very strong, and the plant had 10,000 workers and over 600 staff members, all with good pay. However, as sales gradually declined, the number of staff members has been reduced by half. Besides the commissioners appointed by the construction department, who can earn 200 or 300 yuan per month, the rest only receive a food allowance of nine to forty-five yuan. The number of workers has been reduced to 2,000, and only half of them can work in shifts each day. Their wages are only one dime, which is not enough to feed themselves, let alone support their families. The reason for the mine's downfall is the impact of the Japanese coal dumping policy. Pingxiang coal's sales were primarily for steelmaking in Hanyehping Iron and Coal Company, and for use in major ports and factories along the Yangtze River. Now, Japanese coal is sold cheaply in all these sales locations, and credit is available. Merchants are mostly shortsighted and naturally seek profits. The Commercial Revitalization Commemorative Meeting recently held by Japanese merchants in Hankou is a powerful counter-evidence of this. If Pingxiang coal is in such a state, one can imagine what other industries are like. How do the Chinese people who advocate boycotting foreign goods feel about this?

Pingxiang is located on the western border of Jiangxi Province. Except for the western route from the county seat to Liling along the Pingxiang-Zhuzhou Railway, which is relatively peaceful, the other three routes to the east, south, and north are all mountainous and densely forested, where bandits appear unpredictably. Cars coming from Yichun dare not drive slowly when passing through forests and mountain slopes; they even take risks to speed up, showing how alert they are. Li Tianzhu's bandit gang, with 7,000 guns, uses neighboring Lianhua and Anfuku counties as their base, and frequently harass Shangbu and Nankeng in the southern route of Pingxiang. Recently, they have even spread to the southern countryside of Liling. In the north, Kong Hechong's bandit gang, with 5,000 guns, uses the Shuiyuan area of Wanzai County as their base, and frequently try to infiltrate northern Pingxiang through Huangmao, Cihua, and Tongmu. Recently, they moved most of their bandit troops to the Yangqi Mountain area, and along Banju Mountain and other places, they reached Dapingshan on the border of Pingxiang and Liling. It appears that Li's and Kong's gangs are trying to disrupt the Jiangxi-Hunan transportation. Commissioner Wei of the Administrative District Office said that every county in western Jiangxi has bandits, and the main force is mostly in Yangqiao (belonging to Lianhua). The pseudo-Soviet government is divided into two, one located in the southeast of Jiangxi, and the other located nearby. Even if attacked by 10,000 soldiers, they dare to come out and fight. Everywhere the bandits go, slogans are painted all over the walls. For those that cannot be washed off,

they cleverly add or change one or two words to the existing text. For example, for the slogan "Workers and Peasants' Dictatorship," they add the words "Not Allowed" at the beginning. For the slogan "The Red Army is Fighting for the Interests of the Workers and Peasants," they change the word "Red" to "National." Looking at it, it appears quite dignified. However, for those written in remote and impoverished areas and back alleys, even adding or changing words is impossible, so they can only be eroded by wind and rain.

The Baojia system is quite strict. In addition to the existing organizational rules, at the beginning of the month, the commander of the 62nd Division, stationed in the area, also convened a joint meeting of all Bao heads in the city to instruct the Baojia to seriously reorganize. The agreed terms numbered as many as twenty-eight. If one household violated them, the entire Bao would be implicated. The following are eight of the more serious clauses: (1) Those who refuse to join the Baojia regulations; (2) Those who do not report to the Jia head when suspicious persons sneak in; (3) Those who do not report to the Jia head when visitors from other places stay overnight, or when family members travel overnight and return; (4) Those who do not report to the Jia head when births, deaths, or other events cause changes in the household registration; (5) Those who provide false information when registering their household or arbitrarily destroy their house number; (6) Those who refuse to be drafted into the militia; (7) Those who do not comply with assigned tasks; (8) Those who refuse to pay the Baojia expenses without reason or delay payment without reason. Households that violate any of the above clauses will be fined four to forty yuan. In addition, the land tax and other taxes throughout the county are said to be quite heavy.

The county has little arable land, and food is insufficient, so it is mostly imported from Lianhua or Hunan. Usually, farmers engage in the carting of coal and grain. They are not afraid of the communist bandits, and the communist bandits are said not to rob them. The customs are similar to those of Yichun. In case of disputes, one of the parties usually invites a mediator to comment, called "qi xi" (starting a seat). Then, the other party invites the original mediator or hires others to reconsider, called "fu xi" (returning to the seat). The party who is at fault bears the cost of tea, snacks, and banquets for the mediators' meeting. If the matter is settled fairly, then each party shares half of the cost. Recently, with the establishment of district and township offices, few people voluntarily request them to mediate disputes. To file a complaint with the county government is even rarer. (August 23)

Guangdong Provincial Government Revises Administrative Expenses for Various Counties

丨New Budget to be Implemented from September丨

Guangzhou Dispatch: Recently, the Guangdong Provincial Government has been facing huge expenditures, and various public and military expenses have been increasing without decreasing. Over the years, it has not been able to overcome the trade deficit. According to the latest statistics from the Finance Department, the provincial treasury's income in July was 3,154,312 yuan, and the expenditures were 3,250,811 yuan. In order to reorganize the administrative expenses of various counties in the province and maintain the treasury's currency, the financial authorities have recently revised the new budget for administrative expenses of various counties, which is scheduled to be implemented in September. Currently, the administrative expenses of various counties in Guangdong are: 3,580 yuan per month for first-class counties, 2,872 yuan per month for second-class counties, and 2,068 yuan per month for third-class counties. Among them, simplified third-class counties are only allowed to spend 1,553 yuan per month, and the saved 515 yuan must be submitted for approval and allocated for local construction and conservation projects. The total annual expenditure is 2,929,440 yuan. However, according to the old regulations before April 1931, when county administrative expenses were divided into three classes and five levels, the annual expenditure for administrative expenses of all counties in the province was only 1,386,000 yuan. Compared with the current regulations, the current annual increase is 1,543,434 yuan, which is a huge amount. Therefore, since the implementation of the current regulations in April 1931, the provincial treasury's income has been greatly affected. Counties that previously had grain tax remittances to the treasury have not only had no remittances since then, but have even requested subsidies from the treasury. In order to cope with the situation and solve the difficulties, the authorities have specially ordered the Civil Affairs and Finance Departments to revise the administrative expenses of various counties and reduce them appropriately to save the treasury. The provincial government has issued an order to implement the revised regulations. The new method for county administrative expenses still divides them into three classes: 3,320 yuan per month for first-class counties, 2,710 yuan per month for second-class counties, and 2,048 yuan per month for third-class counties. Simplified third-class counties spend 1,853 yuan per month. According to statistics, there are eighteen first-class counties, twenty-eight second-class counties, forty third-class counties, and eight simplified third-class counties in the province, with a total monthly expenditure of 232,384 yuan and an annual expenditure of 2,788,608 yuan. Compared with the fixed amount of the current regulations, the annual savings will be 140,832 yuan. (August 26)

Current Financial Situation in Hubei Province

This Year's Revenue and Expenditure Budget is Over 19 Million Yuan Each

Revenue and Expenditure in July Show a Surplus of 100,000 Yuan

Wuchang Dispatch: In the past two or three years, Hubei Province has had a monthly deficit, due to higher expenditures and lower revenues. The Finance Department is now striving to balance revenue and expenditure. In the past few months, it has been able to balance revenue and expenditure. Furthermore, Finance Department Director Jia Shiyi traveled to various counties in western Hubei, convened meetings, and reorganized taxes. Therefore, the provincial treasury's revenue and expenditure in July, showed a surplus of 100,000 yuan. The revenue and expenditure figures for July are as follows:

Revenue: Land tax: 534,808.080 yuan; Deed tax: 21,021.92 yuan; Business tax: 248,310.681 yuan; Brokerage tax: 6,355.000 yuan; Slaughter tax: 13,950.400 yuan; House tax: 11,544.780 yuan; Various rents: 13,227.970 yuan; Operating income: 110,372.600 yuan; Subsidies: 605,000.000 yuan; Securities income: 1,580.000 yuan; Regular and additional taxes: 10,977.490 yuan; Miscellaneous income: 105,535.679 yuan; Budget surplus: 14,717.480 yuan; Public bond proceeds: 157,037.550 yuan; Borrowings: 60,000.000 yuan; Suspense account: 2,130.480 yuan; Advances: 20,297.380 yuan; Accumulated surplus: 16,708,273.0 yuan; Total revenue: 1,574,491.220 yuan.

Expenditure: Repayment of borrowings: 220,000.000 yuan; Suspense account: 400.270 yuan; Advances: 12,970.000 yuan; Party affairs expenses: 10,637.840 yuan; Administrative expenses: 63,863.330 yuan; Judicial expenses: 86,110.060 yuan; Public security expenses: 175,970.500 yuan; Finance expenses: 69,102.420 yuan; Education and culture expenses: 224,146.800 yuan; Industry expenses: 29,989.220 yuan; Transportation expenses: 20,650.090 yuan; Health expenses: 1,726.220 yuan; Construction expenses: 66,012.130 yuan; Assistance expenses: 630.000 yuan; Government business capital: 108,391.270 yuan; Bandit suppression expenses: 198,036.220 yuan; Contingency fund: 73,318.220 yuan; Interest: 2,380.000 yuan; Total expenditure: 1,467,944.144 yuan.

The surplus after offsetting revenue and expenditure is 106,547.080 yuan. In addition, 60,000 yuan was borrowed to repay 220,000 yuan of old debt, with a net repayment of 160,000 yuan. Furthermore, bandit suppression expenses were over 190,000 yuan, which is more than in other months. The Finance Department believes that since FY 1933 has already begun, the province's annual revenue and expenditure budget for this year, based on the General Headquarters' approved FY 1933 revenue and expenditure summary and the provincial government's approved measures, has been compiled. The revenue and expenditure budget is over 19 million yuan each. The special revenue and expenditure budget is 500,000 yuan each. The compilation has been completed and will be submitted to the provincial government along with the opinions of various agencies for review by the Commander-in-Chief. (August 31)

Jiangsu Province Rectifies Deed Tax

丨Township Offices Assist in Rectification丨

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The Jiangsu Finance Department believes that there are rampant abuses in the deed tax collection of various counties, so it has drafted ten rectification measures to be followed by all counties. The measures are as follows: (1) Jiangsu Province formulates these measures to rectify the deed tax of various counties, and entrusts various township offices to assist in handling deed tax matters; (2) Each county shall designate township offices as sales and issuance points for deed paper. The county government shall determine the number of papers to be sold in advance and distribute them to the offices for residents to purchase nearby; (3) Each township office that sells deed paper shall keep separate monthly records for review by the county government. It shall also issue the aforementioned report book at any time, or the Finance Department shall issue it to each county. A supplementary register shall also be set up to list the number of sold deed papers, the name and address of the purchaser, so as to urge tax payments, without omission; (4) Before the promulgation of the notary law, residents of each county who buy or pawn real estate may use the head and deputy of each township office as notaries to sign and seal the contract, and may extract 20% of the original brokerage fee to supplement the expenses of the township office; (5) After the implementation of these measures, the deed paper of residents in each county who buy or pawn real estate must be signed and sealed by a notary. The county government may issue the tax deed to the head and deputy of the district town where the deed is located to sign and seal it as a notary, but no brokerage fee may be extracted; (6) The head and deputy of each township office shall investigate the households that buy or pawn real estate in their jurisdiction at any time. In addition to ordering them to purchase official deed paper, they shall urge and list the households that have not paid taxes within the time limit and report them monthly. The county government shall send personnel to jointly inspect and urge tax payment; (7) The head and deputy of each township office shall be responsible for leading the county government personnel to inspect the unpaid deed paper of each household; (8) Each county and township shall persuade and correct the use of official deed paper or the short writing of contract prices. If there is any collusion, they shall be punished according to law after being discovered; (9) The head and deputy of each county and township office shall sign and seal the official deed paper purchased by residents who buy or pawn real estate, and collect the paper price and brokerage fee separately according to regulations. They shall not extort extra money. Those who violate this shall be reported and investigated and dealt with according to law; (10) These measures shall be implemented after being approved by the Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee.

Suzhou

Standards for the Appointment of Trial Officials

The High Court announced the standards for the appointment of trial officials in various counties, including two points: (1) Those who pass the trial official examination; (2) Those who have studied law and political science in a university for more than three years and have a diploma, or have served as judicial trial officials and have been qualified by the court. The appointment method is to first submit documents proving qualifications for review. If they match, they will be ordered to draft a civil and criminal judgment each in court and submit them to the civil and criminal courts for grading. Only those who pass the grade will be registered for appointment. Those who have graduated from school but have not handled judicial affairs, or who have less experience, must be ordered to study in local courts for five or six months. After the performance is assessed to be excellent, they will be appointed at the discretion of the court. No matter which school recommends them or who introduces them, they shall not be appointed without going through this appointment procedure.

Completion of the Tianping Mountain Road

The new Tianping Mountain Road in Mudu, starting from Xiahechang in the town and ending at the foot of Tianping Mountain, with a total length of 1,500 feet, has been completed. The opening ceremony is scheduled for September 10. To admire Fan Zhongyan, it has been named Jingfan Road.

Bandit Gangs Rampage in the Four Townships Around Taihu Lake

In the Paotaiwan area of ​​Pingwang Township, Wujiang County, three bandit ships arrived on the evening of the 31st, carrying more than 40 bandits with complete firearms. They intended to rob the shops in Pingwang Town. After the water police stationed in Fan Town learned about it, they immediately sent a team to suppress them. The bandits had already fled to West Taihu Lake after hearing the news. It is also reported that two bandit ships were found in Xihua Township in Suxiang on the same day, carrying more than ten bandits. They stayed for about an hour before leaving. In addition, a Suzhou rice boat, carrying more than 50 "shi" of rice, was robbed near Huangtiandang while heading to Kunshan, with a loss of about 200 yuan.

Judgment on the Trademark Infringement Case of Shi De Zhi

Lu Jianfang, the owner of the Laodeji Pharmacy at the Shilu intersection outside the city gate, sold Jizhongshui and other medicines in the name of the Shanghai Shidezhi Pharmacy. After Shidezhi discovered this, they filed a lawsuit with the Wuxian District Court, and Lu was arrested and detained. The judgment has been issued yesterday. Lu Jianfang knowingly sold goods with counterfeit trademarks and trade names and was sentenced to two months of imprisonment and ordered to compensate for business losses of fifty yuan.

Wuxi

Postponement of Land Value Tax for One Month

County Magistrate Yan Shenyu received an order from the Finance Department to clear and remit all of the first installment of land value tax by the end of August. However, the deadline has now passed, and the payment is not very enthusiastic, because the weather has been dry and the farmers are watering the fields day and night, making them miserable. Therefore, he specially sent a telegram to the Finance Department to request a postponement of one month from September 1st to September 31st. If the payment is overdue, a late payment penalty of 10% will be charged. Yesterday, the Finance Department approved the telegram, and County Magistrate Yan announced it to the public. At the same time, the Finance Department, in order to expedite the payment of old debts from previous years, specially sent Commissioner Wang Xunyuan to various counties to supervise the payment. Yesterday, the county government of this county was also instructed to inform Commissioner Wang, who will come to Wuxi in the coming days.

Autumn Cocoon Market Opens on Time

This year's autumn silkworms were immersed in acid earlier, so those that went on the frames earlier have been there for five or six days. The rest will go on the frames today or tomorrow. However, since the beginning of autumn, there have been thunderstorms every morning, and it has been as sultry as before. When the silkworms on the frames hear thunder, some crawl out of their cocoons and die on the frames, and some die in the cocoons, causing them to rot, resulting in huge losses. Now, a certain silk factory's test reeling of autumn cocoons shows that 650 "jin" (a Chinese unit of weight, about 0.5 kg) of cocoons are needed to make one "dan" (a Chinese unit of weight, about 50 kg) of silk, which is six to ten times more than spring cocoons. The price of mulberry leaves in the four townships is very expensive, with the highest price being five yuan per "dan". The Wuxi Cocoon Industry Association held a general meeting of members yesterday (1st) at 3:00 PM at the Xujialong Association. The meeting, chaired by Hua Shaochun, decided to set September 4th as the opening date for the market. The opening price for cocoons is set at 35 yuan.

Changshu

Disputes in the County Chamber of Commerce Have Not Ended

The election of executive and supervisory committee members of the County Chamber of Commerce on the 22nd of last month was marred by fraudulent activities perpetrated by Wu Zhongying, the supervisory election member, during the drawing of lots. Wu marked the bamboo sticks with various symbols such as "light," "hairy," "wide," "narrow," "long," and "short." However, his technique was not clever, and he was discovered by Tang Xinfu, a representative of the silver and money industry. The whole place was in an uproar, and the social community was shocked. For a while, it caused a sensation in society, and the entire silver and money industry withdrew from the Chamber of Commerce. The bamboo sticks were sealed and stored in the county government. Since then, the new executive and supervisory committee members have been stalled. Wu Zhongying, who engaged in fraudulent activities, has been trying to mediate because he has a great relationship with the matter. The other day, County Magistrate Zhou Heng personally visited Zhenye Bank to discuss the matter with Cui Junru and Tang Xinfu, representatives of the silver and money industry, and advised them to compromise in order to resolve the matter peacefully. The representatives refused to accept, saying that unless the Chamber of Commerce is re-elected or the fraudulent person is severely investigated, they will not rejoin the Chamber of Commerce. As a result, County Magistrate Zhou returned quickly. The new executive and supervisory committee members of the Chamber of Commerce, in addition to reporting to the High Court themselves, are also continuing to elect standing committee members and chairmen, etc. The date has been set for September 2nd, and the county has been asked to send personnel to supervise.

Local News

Shanghai Already Within Hurricane Zone

Two Hurricanes Converge and Advance Northward

Customs Guns Fired, Ocean Liners Suspended

The Ta Mei Wan Pao (Shanghai Times) reports that two hurricanes in the East China Sea, located at 26 degrees north latitude and 125 degrees east longitude, north of the Miyako Islands, are "getting married" this morning (the 1st). They are then heading northwest-west, apparently intending to spend their honeymoon near Shanghai. If the current direction remains unchanged, they will touch the coast slightly north of Wenzhou tonight. However, hurricanes appearing outside the Chinese coast often veer to the right. If that happens, the center point may reach Shanghai, which is not impossible. Judging from the current situation, proceeding at a speed of 20 miles per hour, it will reach a certain coastal area before midnight. The strength of the wind is not yet certain. Shanghai is now within the hurricane zone. The intermittent wind and rain today are a precursor to the hurricane's arrival. Ships in the Shanghai area have received warnings for precautionary measures. The Xujiahui Observatory and the Huangpu Beach Wind Signal Station are working day and night to report the progress of the hurricane to ship captains and owners. Vessels outside the coasts of Fujian, Zhejiang, and Jiangsu are currently experiencing extremely bad weather.

Observatory Report

The Xujiahui Observatory reported at 9:00 AM on the 1st that the severe hurricane in the southern East China Sea is rapidly moving northwest-west or northwest. At 4:30 PM on the same day, it reported cloudy skies and showers or storms along the coast. The hurricane is clearly moving northwest-west, approaching the coast between Wenzhou and Shanghai, and will likely make landfall around Ningbo. The weather in the East China Sea and along the coast is very bad. There are strong easterly to north-easterly winds in the Yellow Sea. The atmospheric pressure east of the Philippines remains low. At 2:00 PM, the center point of the hurricane was within 60 miles of the intersection of 27 degrees north latitude and 125 degrees east longitude, moving northwest with severe winds. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM today, the temperature in Shanghai reached a high of 87.8 and a low of 75.5. On the same day last year, the high was 71.6 and the low was 66.0.

Jianghai Customs Warning

At 4:30 PM yesterday, Jianghai Customs received a further weather report,

knowing that strong winds and rain are heading toward Shanghai, with even greater hurricanes along the Zhejiang coast. Therefore, a cannon was fired to signal the impending major hurricane, to warn the commercial ships and small boats on the Huangpu River to take precautions and avoid disaster. After firing the cannon, a large black warning ball was also raised on the roof of the Customs House, doubled, indicating the severity of the hurricane's impact on Shanghai. The Huangpu River has been taking on a storm-preparation atmosphere since 5:00 PM.

Shanghai-Ningbo Ships Suspended

After the Customs opened the hurricane warning cannon and hung two black balls, the shipping companies in Shanghai immediately notified all ocean liners in port that those scheduled to depart should all suspend operations as a precaution. Yesterday, the Ningbo liners "New Beijing" and "New Ning Shao," etc., had already loaded their cargo, and passengers had boarded, ready to depart for Ningbo. Upon receiving this warning, the ships received orders from their companies and dared not risk sailing. They immediately notified the passengers to disembark and refund their tickets, declaring that they would not sail due to the storm. For a time, the Taikoo and Ning Shao docks were crowded with passengers seeking refunds.

Zhejiang Sea Ships All Blocked

Commercial ships sailing from Shanghai to the Zhejiang coast, such as those on the Wenzhou-Taizhou line, the Zhoushan line, and the Ruiping line, typically depart around 5:00 PM. Yesterday, these sampans received news of the hurricane approaching Shanghai and being even stronger along the Zhejiang coast. All ships to Zhejiang also suspended operations. Those that had already sailed

were telegraphed to anchor in Wusong to avoid the storm. The departure dates for ships to the north and south seas were also postponed by the shipping companies until today.

Huangpu River on Alert

All small steamers, cargo boats, and tugboats on the Huangpu River, from 5:00 PM yesterday, followed the warning from Jianghai Customs, stopped operations early, and sailed to the Suzhou Creek or docked at the wharves to prevent accidents. Therefore, after 5:30 PM, the Huangpu River was quiet as ships prepared for the storm, and there were very few vessels traveling to and fro.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Handles Registration Matters

Acting as Agent for Four Types of Registration Procedures

Established a Registration Department to Handle Matters

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce issued a special notice yesterday regarding the handling of registration matters, stating: "The registration of trademarks and other matters relates to commercial interests. However, merchants often neglect them because they are not familiar with the procedures. In particular, the registration of companies is clearly stipulated by law and cannot be avoided. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce, for the purpose of strict supervision, has repeatedly ordered all companies to register in accordance with the law within a deadline, and has stated that companies already established but not yet registered by September 30th of this year will be punished according to law and strictly banned once discovered. The deadline is approaching. All companies that have been established but have not yet registered should rush to complete the registration procedures to avoid violating the law. In order to safeguard the interests of merchants and to facilitate the registration of members and non-members of the Chamber of Commerce, we have established a registration department, which will begin acting as an agent for four types of procedures from September 10th: trademark registration, company registration, commercial registration, and bank registration. For inquiries or requests for agency, please contact the registration department of the Chamber of Commerce. We hereby notify you."

Brief Stop in Nanjing, Then to Jiangxi to Meet Chiang

Song Visited Huang Fu Yesterday Morning to Continue Discussing Finances

This is an over-cautious preparation by the authorities of various countries." Mr. Tang entered Nanjing last night.

Entered Nanjing Last Night
